Task instruction sent to agent 
Trace the Kubernetes Container Runtime Interface (CRI) from its gRPC service definition to containerd's implementation

The Kubernetes CRI defines a gRPC RuntimeService in its api.proto file. Trace the complete interface contract:
1. Find the CRI RuntimeService gRPC definition in the kubernetes repo (under staging/src/k8s.io/cri-api/)
2. Identify the key RPC methods (RunPodSandbox, StopPodSandbox, RemovePodSandbox, etc.)
3. Find where containerd implements these CRI methods
4. Document how kubernetes vendors containerd's API types (check kubernetes/vendor/github.com/containerd/)

Your analysis must span both the kubernetes and containerd source trees under /ccb_crossrepo/src/.
Write your findings to REASONING.md in the workspace.

Look for:

Provide file paths with line numbers for the key implementation methods.

37-usertool_resultRead
   150→    // PullImage pulls an image with authentication config.
   151→    rpc PullImage(PullImageRequest) returns (PullImageResponse) {}
   152→    // RemoveImage removes the image.
   153→    // This call is idempotent, and must not return an error if the image has
   154→    // already been removed.
   155→    // Note that if the image is referenced by multiple tags (even across different repositories
   156→    // if they resolve to the same image digest), removing the image by a single tag
   157→    // will remove all of its tags. For example, if `repo/image:v1` and `another_repo/image:latest`
   158→    // point to the same image, removing `repo/image:v1` will also remove `another_repo/image:latest`.
   159→    // The next call to ListImages, ImageStatus, ImageFsInfo will not return this image.
   160→    // The resources (e.g. disk space) may be cleaned asynchronously
   161→    // and not guaranteed to be cleaned up by the time this method returns.
   162→    rpc RemoveImage(RemoveImageRequest) returns (RemoveImageResponse) {}
   163→    // ImageFSInfo returns information of the filesystem that is used to store images.
   164→    // Usage information may include images that were removed, but are still being cleaned up.
   165→    rpc ImageFsInfo(ImageFsInfoRequest) returns (ImageFsInfoResponse) {}
   166→}
   167→
   168→message VersionRequest {
   169→    // Version of the kubelet runtime API.
   170→    string version = 1;
   171→}
   172→
   173→message VersionResponse {
   174→    // Version of the kubelet runtime API.
   175→    string version = 1;
   176→    // Name of the container runtime.
   177→    string runtime_name = 2;
   178→    // Version of the container runtime. The string must be
   179→    // semver-compatible.
   180→    string runtime_v
... (truncated)

    33→// StopPodSandbox stops the sandbox. If there are any running containers in the
    34→// sandbox, they should be forcibly terminated.
    35→func (c *criService) StopPodSandbox(ctx context.Context, r *runtime.StopPodSandboxRequest) (*runtime.StopPodSandboxResponse, error) {
    36→	span := tracing.SpanFromContext(ctx)
    37→	sandbox, err := c.sandboxStore.Get(r.GetPodSandboxId())
    38→	if err != nil {
    39→		if !errdefs.IsNotFound(err) {
    40→			return nil, fmt.Errorf("an error occurred when try to find sandbox %q: %w",
    41→				r.GetPodSandboxId(), err)
    42→		}
    43→
    44→		// The StopPodSandbox RPC is idempotent, and must not return an error

   858→message LinuxContainerResources {
   859→    // CPU CFS (Completely Fair Scheduler) period. Default: 0 (not specified).
   860→    int64 cpu_period = 1;
   861→    // CPU CFS (Completely Fair Scheduler) quota. Default: 0 (not specified).
   862→    int64 cpu_quota = 2;
   863→    // CPU shares (relative weight vs. other containers). Default: 0 (not specified).
   864→    int64 cpu_shares = 3;
   865→    // Memory limit in bytes. Default: 0 (not specified).
   866→    int64 memory_limit_in_bytes = 4;
   867→    // OOMScoreAdj adjusts the oom-killer score. Default: 0 (not specified).
   868→    int64 oom_score_adj = 5;
   869→    // CpusetCpus constrains the allowed set of logical CPUs. Default: "" (not specified).
   870→    string cpuset_cpus = 6;
   871→    // CpusetMems constrains the allowed set of memory nodes. Default: "" (not specified).
   872→    string cpuset_mems = 7;
   873→    // List of HugepageLimits to limit the HugeTLB usage of container per page size. Default: nil (not specified).
   874→    repeated HugepageLimit hugepage_limits = 8;
   875→    // Unified resources for cgroup v2. Default: nil (not specified).
   876→    // Each key/value in the map refers to the cgroup v2.

   878→    map<string, string> unified = 9;
   879→    // Memory swap limit in bytes. Default 0 (not specified).
   880→    int64 memory_swap_limit_in_bytes = 10;
   881→}

    26→option go_package = "github.com/containerd/containerd/api/services/containers/v1;containers";
    27→
    28→// Containers provides metadata storage for containers used in the execution
    29→// service.
    30→//
    31→// The objects here provide an state-independent view of containers for use in
    32→// management and resource pinning. From that perspective, containers do not
    33→// have a "state" but rather this is the set of resources that will be
    34→// considered in use by the container.
    35→//
    36→// From the perspective of the execution service, these objects represent the

    25→// Mount describes mounts for a container.
    26→//
    27→// This type is the lingua franca of ContainerD. All services provide mounts
    28→// to be used with the container at creation time.
    29→//
    30→// The Mount type follows the structure of the mount syscall, including a type,
    31→// source, target and options.
    32→message Mount {
    33→	// Type defines the nature of the mount.
    34→	string type = 1;
    35→
    36→	// Source specifies the name of the mount. Depending on mount type, this
    37→	// may be a volume name or a host path, or even ignored.
    38→	string source = 2;
    39→
    40→	// Target path in container
    41→	string target = 3;
    42→
    43→	// Options specifies zero or more fstab style mount options.
    44→	repeated string options = 4;
    45→}
    46→
    47→message ActiveMount {
    48→	Mount mount = 1;

package containerd.types;

import "google/protobuf/any.proto";

option go_package = "github.com/containerd/containerd/api/types;types";

message RuntimeRequest {
	string runtime_path = 1;
	// Options correspond to CreateTaskRequest.options.
	// This is needed to pass the runc binary path, etc.
	google.protobuf.Any options = 2;
}

message RuntimeVersion {
	string version = 1;
	string revision = 2;
}

message RuntimeInfo {
	string name = 1;
	RuntimeVersion version = 2;
	// Options correspond to RuntimeInfoRequest.Options (contains runc binary path, etc.)
	google.protobuf.Any options = 3;
	// OCI-compatible runtimes should use https://github.com/opencontainers/runtime-spec/blob/main/features.md
	google.protobuf.Any features = 4;
	// Annotations of the shim. Irrelevant to features.Annotations.
	map<string, string> annotations = 5;
}

## Summary

The analysis traced the Kubernetes Container Runtime Interface (CRI) through three key areas:

### 1. CRI gRPC Definition (Kubernetes)
- **Location:** `staging/src/k8s.io/cri-api/pkg/apis/runtime/v1/api.proto`
- **RuntimeService:** 29 RPC methods covering pod sandbox management, container lifecycle, execution/streaming, statistics, and runtime configuration
- Key methods documented with line numbers: `RunPodSandbox`, `StopPodSandbox`, `RemovePodSandbox`, `CreateContainer`, `StartContainer`, `StopContainer`, `RemoveContainer`, etc.

### 2. containerd CRI Implementation
- **Location:** `internal/cri/server/`
- Implementation files identified for each major method:
  - `sandbox_run.go` (RunPodSandbox at line 53)
  - `sandbox_stop.go` (StopPodSandbox at line 35)
  - `sandbox_remove.go` (RemovePodSandbox at line 34)
  - `container_create.go` (CreateContainer at line 60)
  - `container_start.go` (StartContainer at line 45)
  - `container_stop.go` (StopContainer at line 39)
  - `container_remove.go` (RemoveContainer at line 34)
- The `criService` struct integrates with sandboxStore, containerStore, CNI networking, and NRI plugins

### 3. Kubernetes Vendored containerd Types
- **Location:** `vendor/github.com/containerd/`
- 5 packages vendored: containerd (API), errdefs, log, ttrpc, typeurl
- Core type definitions: sandbox.proto, mount.proto, task.proto, descriptor.proto, platform.proto
- Service definitions: Containers Service (181 lines), Tasks Service (227 lines), Version Service (33 lines)
- Shows how CRI operations map to containerd's native Containers and Tasks gRPC services

SUPPORTING PACKAGES\n\n#### errdefs/ (Error Definitions)\n- **errors.go**: Common error types mapping to gRPC status codes:\n  - Unknown, InvalidArgument, NotFound, AlreadyExists, PermissionDenied\n  - ResourceExhausted, FailedPrecondition, Conflict, NotModified\n  - Aborted, OutOfRange, NotImplemented, Internal\n  - Unavailable, DataLoss, Unauthenticated\n\n- **pkg/errgrpc/**: gRPC error conversion utilities\n- **pkg/internal/**: Internal error type utilities\n\n#### ttrpc/ (TTRPC Protocol)\n- **48 Go files** implementing timeserving RPC protocol\n- Alternative to gRPC for container runtime communication\n- Features: client.go, server.go, channel.go, request.proto\n- Unix socket support (unixcreds_linux.go)\n- Provides streaming and unary RPC capabilities\n\n#### typeurl/ (Type URL Registry)\n- **v2/types.go**: Protocol buffer Any type marshaling/unmarshaling\n- Maintains type registry for dynamic type resolution\n- Supports custom handlers for message serialization\n\n#### log/\n- **context.go**: Logging context utilities for containerd operations\n\n### 4. tracking\n3. **Labels/Metadata**: String maps for arbitrary key-value associations\n4. **Modular Services**: Separate container metadata (Containers) from task execution (Tasks)\n5. **Field Masks**: 489\u2192// volumeMounts sets up image volumes for container. Rely on the removal of container\n   490\u2192// root directory to do cleanup. Note that image volume will be skipped, if there is criMounts\n   491\u2192// specified with the same destination.\n   492\u2192func (c *criService) volumeMounts(platform imagespec.Platform, containerRootDir string, containerConfig *runtime.ContainerConfig, config *imagespec.ImageConfig) []*runtime.Mount {\n   493\u2192\tvar uidMappings, gidMappings []*runtime.IDMapping\n   494\u2192\tif platform.OS == \"linux\" {\n   495\u2192\t\tif usernsOpts := containerConfig.GetLinux().GetSecurityContext().GetNamespaceOptions().GetUsernsOptions(); usernsOpts != nil {\n   496\u2192\t\t\tuidMappings = usernsOpts.GetUids()\n   497\u2192\t\t\tgidMappings = usernsOpts.GetGids()\n   498\u2192\t\t}\n   499\u2192\t}\n   500\u2192\n   501\u2192\tcriMounts := containerConfig.GetMounts()\n   502\u2192\n   503\u2192\tif len(config.Volumes) == 0 {\n   504\u2192\t\treturn nil\n   505\u2192\t}\n   506\u2192\tvar mounts []*runtime.Mount\n   507\u2192\tfor dst := range config.Volumes {\n   508\u2192\t\tif isInCRIMounts(dst, criMounts) {\n   509\u2192\t\t\t// Skip the image volume, if there is CRI defined volume mapping.\n   510\u2192\t\t\t// TODO(random-liu): This should be handled by Kubelet in the future.\n   511\u2192\t\t\t// Kubelet should decide what to use for image volume, and also de-duplicate\n   512\u2192\t\t\t// the image volume and user mounts.\n   513\u2192\t\t\tcontinue\n   514\u2192\t\t}\n   515\u2192\t\tvolumeID := util.GenerateID()\n   516\u2192\t\tsrc := filepath.Join(containerRootDir, \"volumes\", volumeID)\n   517\u2192\t\t// When the platform OS is Linux, ensure dst is a _Linux_ abs path.\n   518\u2192\t\t// We can't use filepath.IsAbs() because, when executing on Windows, it checks for\n   519\u2192\t\t// Windows abs paths.\n   520\u2192\t\tif platform.OS == \"linux\" && !strings.HasPrefix(dst, \"/\") {\n   521\u2192\t\t\t// On Windows, ToSlash() is needed to ensure the path is a valid Linux path.\n   522\u2192\t\t\t// On Linux, ToSlash() is a no-op.\n   523\u2192\t\t\toldDst := dst\n   524\u2192\t\t\tdst = filepath.ToSlash(filepath.Join(\"/\", dst))\n   525\u2192\t\t\tlog.L.Debugf(\"Volume destination %q is not absolute, converted to %q\", oldDst, dst)\n   526\u2192\t\t}\n   527\u2192\t\t// addOCIBindMounts will create these volumes.\n   528\u2192\t\tmounts = append(mounts, &runtime.Mount{\n   529\u2192\t\t\tContainerPath:  dst,\n   530\u2192\t\t\tHostPath:       src,\n   531\u2192\t\t\tSelinuxRelabel: true,\n   532\u2192\t\t\tUidMappings:    uidMappings,\n   533\u2192\t\t\tGidMappings:    gidMappings,\n   534\u2192\t\t})\n   535\u2192\t}\n   536\u2192\treturn mounts\n   537\u2192}\n   538\u2192\n   539\u2192// runtimeSpec returns a default runtime spec used in cri-containerd.\n   540\u2192func (c *criService) runtimeSpec(id string, platform imagespec.Platform, baseSpecFile string, opts ...oci.SpecOpts) (*runtimespec.Spec, error) {\n   541\u2192\t// GenerateSpec needs namespace.\n   542\u2192\tctx := util.NamespacedContext()\n   543\u2192\tcontainer := &containers.Container{ID: id}\n   544\u2192\n   545\u2192\tif baseSpecFile != \"\" {\n   546\u2192\t\tbaseSpec, err := c.LoadOCISpec(baseSpecFile)\n   547\u2192\t\tif err != nil {\n   548\u2192\t\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"can't load base OCI spec %q: %w\", baseSpecFile, err)\n   549\u2192\t\t}\n   550\u2192\n   551\u2192\t\tspec := oci.Spec{}\n   552\u2192\t\tif err := util.DeepCopy(&spec, &baseSpec); err != nil {\n   553\u2192\t\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"failed to clone OCI spec: %w\", err)\n   554\u2192\t\t}\n   555\u2192\n   556\u2192\t\t// Fix up cgroups path\n   557\u2192\t\tapplyOpts := append([]oci.SpecOpts{oci.WithNamespacedCgroup()}, opts...)\n   558\u2192\n 562\u2192\n   563\u2192\t\treturn &spec, nil\n   564\u2192\t}\n   565\u2192\n   566\u2192\tspec, err := oci.GenerateSpecWithPlatform(ctx, nil, platforms.Format(platform), container, opts...)\n   567\u2192\tif err != nil {\n   568\u2192\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"failed to generate spec: %w\", err)\n   569\u2192\t}\n   570\u2192\n   571\u2192\treturn spec, nil\n   572\u2192}\n   573\u2192\n   574\u2192const (\n   575\u2192\t// relativeRootfsPath is the rootfs path relative to bundle path.\n   576\u2192\trelativeRootfsPath = \"rootfs\"\n   577\u2192\t// hostnameEnv is the key for HOSTNAME env.\n   578\u2192\thostnameEnv = \"HOSTNAME\"\n   579\u2192)\n   580\u2192\n   581\u2192// platformSpecOpts adds additional runtime spec options that may rely on\n   582\u2192// runtime information (rootfs mounted), or platform specific checks with\n   583\u2192// no defined workaround (yet) to specify for other platforms.\n   584\u2192func (c *criService) platformSpecOpts(\n   585\u2192\tplatform imagespec.Platform,\n   586\u2192\tconfig *runtime.ContainerConfig,\n   587\u2192\timageConfig *imagespec.ImageConfig,\n   588\u2192) ([]oci.SpecOpts, error) {\n   589\u2192\tvar specOpts []oci.SpecOpts\n   590\u2192\n   591\u2192\t// First deal with the set of options we can use across platforms currently.\n   592\u2192\t// Linux user strings have workarounds on other platforms to avoid needing to\n   593\u2192\t// mount the rootfs, but on Linux hosts it must be mounted\n   594\u2192\t//\n   595\u2192\t// TODO(dcantah): I think the seccomp package can be made to compile on\n   596\u2192\t// !linux and used here as well.\n   597\u2192\tif platform.OS == \"linux\" {\n   598\u2192\t\t// Set container username. This could only be done by containerd, because it needs\n   599\u2192\t\t// access to the container rootfs. Pass user name to containerd, and let it overwrite\n   600\u2192\t\t// the spec for us.\n   601\u2192\t\tsecurityContext := config.GetLinux().GetSecurityContext()\n   602\u2192\t\tuserstr, err := util.GenerateUserString(\n   603\u2192\t\t\tsecurityContext.GetRunAsUsername(),\n   604\u2192\t\t\tsecurityContext.GetRunAsUser(),\n   605\u2192\t\t\tsecurityContext.GetRunAsGroup())\n   606\u2192\t\tif err != nil {\n   607\u2192\t\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"failed to generate user string: %w\", err)\n   608\u2192\t\t}\n   609\u2192\t\tif userstr == \"\" {\n   610\u2192\t\t\t// Lastly, since no user override was passed via CRI try to set via OCI\n   611\u2192\t\t\t// Image\n   612\u2192\t\t\tuserstr = imageConfig.User\n   613\u2192\t\t}\n   614\u2192\t\tif userstr != \"\" {\n   615\u2192\t\t\tspecOpts = append(specOpts, oci.WithUser(userstr))\n   616\u2192\t\t}\n   617\u2192\t}\n   618\u2192\n   619\u2192\t// Now grab the truly platform specific options (seccomp, apparmor etc. for linux\n   620\u2192\t// for example).\n   621\u2192\tctrSpecOpts, err := c.containerSpecOpts(config, imageConfig)\n   622\u2192\tif err != nil {\n   623\u2192\t\treturn nil, err\n   624\u2192\t}\n   625\u2192\tspecOpts = append(specOpts, ctrSpecOpts...)\n   626\u2192\n   627\u2192\treturn specOpts, nil\n   628\u2192}\n   629\u2192\n   630\u2192// buildContainerSpec build container's OCI spec depending on controller's target platform OS.\n   631\u2192func (c *criService) buildContainerSpec(\n   632\u2192\tplatform imagespec.Platform,\n   633\u2192\tid string,\n   634\u2192\tsandboxID string,\n   635\u2192\tsandboxPid uint32,\n   636\u2192\tnetNSPath string,\n   637\u2192\tcontainerName string,\n   638\u2192\timageName string,\n   639\u2192\tconfig file`hugetlb.<hugepagesize>.limit_in_byte` in container level cgroup.\n   884\u2192// For example, `PageSize=1GB`, `Limit=1073741824` means setting `1073741824` bytes to hugetlb.1GB.limit_in_bytes.\n 904\u2192// If a capability is added to only the add_capabilities list then it gets added to permitted,\n   905\u2192// inheritable, effective and bounding sets, i.e. all sets except the ambient set.\n   906\u2192// If a capability is added to only the add_ambient_capabilities list then it gets added to all sets, i.e permitted\n   907\u2192// inheritable, effective, bounding and ambient sets.\n   908\u2192// If a capability is added to add_capabilities and add_ambient_capabilities lists then it gets added to all sets, i.e.\n   909\u2192// permitted, inheritable, effective, bounding 918\u2192\n   919\u2192// LinuxContainerSecurityContext holds linux security configuration that will be applied to a container.\n   920\u2192message LinuxContainerSecurityContext {\n   921\u2192    // covering:\n- **Pod Sandbox lifecycle:** Create, start, stop, remove sandboxes\n- **Container lifecycle:** Create, start, stop, remove containers\n- **Execution:** Sync/async exec, attach, port forwarding\n- **Monitoring:** Stats, events, metrics\n- **Configuration:** Runtime status and updates\n\ncontainerd implements this interface through its `criService` in the `internal/cri/server/` package, translating CRI calls to containerd's native APIs (Containers Service, Tasks Service) while managing state through internal stores and integrating with CNI for networking and NRI for resource management hooks.\n\nKubernetes vendors containerd's core API types and supporting packages (errdefs, ttrpc, typeurl) to enable direct communication with containerd daemons through well-defined gRPC/TTRPC service boundaries.\n",

implement.\n\n```\n\u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510\n\u2502 patterns:\n1. **State Management:** Uses `sandboxStore` and `containerStore` for lifecycle tracking\n2. **Sandbox Service Integration:** Delegates execution to `sandboxService`\n3. **NRI Integration:** Calls Node Resource Interface plugins at lifecycle events\n4. **Network Management:** Handles CNI networking for pod sandboxes\n5. **Event Generation:** Sends container events (CREATED, STARTED, DELETED)\n6. **Error Handling:** Includes retry logic for transient failures\n\n---\n\n## Part 3: Kubernetes Vendored containerd API Types\n\n### Location\n\n**Directory:** `/ccb_crossrepo/src/kubernetes/vendor/github.com/containerd/`\n\n### Vendored Packages\n\nKubernetes vendors **5 main containerd packages**:\n\n```\nvendor/github.com/containerd/\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 metadata:\n- ID, runtime, spec, labels\n- Timestamps, extensions\n\n#### `api/types/mount.proto` (65 lines)\nDescribes filesystem mounts:\n- `Mount`: type, source, target, options\n- `ActiveMount`: mount with timestamp and mount point metadata\n- `ActivationInfo`: activation state with mounts\n\n#### `api/types/task/task.proto`\nProcess and task metadata:\n- `Status` enum: UNKNOWN, CREATED, RUNNING, STOPPED, PAUSED, PAUSING\n- `Process`: container_id, pid, status, stdio, exit_status\n- `ProcessInfo`: process ID and platform-specific info\n\n#### `api/types/descriptor.proto` (33 lines)\nOCI blob descriptors:\n- media_type, digest, size, annotations\n\n#### `api/types/platform.proto` (30 lines)\nOCI platform specification:\n- os, architecture, variant, os_version\n\n### ResourceExhausted, FailedPrecondition\n- Conflict, NotModified, Aborted, OutOfRange\n- NotImplemented, Internal, Unavailable, DataLoss, Unauthenticated\n\n#### ttrpc/\nAlternative to gRPC for Mapping\n\n### How CRI Operations Map to containerd Services\n\n| CRI Operation | containerd Service | containerd Method |\n|---------------|-------------------|-------------------|\n| `CreateContainer` | Containers + Tasks | `Containers.Create` + `Tasks.Create` |\n| `StartContainer` | Tasks | `Tasks.Start` |\n| `StopContainer` | Tasks | `Tasks.Kill` |\n| `RemoveContainer` | Containers + Tasks | `Tasks.Delete` + `Containers.Delete` |\n| `ListContainers` | Containers + Tasks | `Containers.List` + `Tasks.List` |\n| `ContainerStats` | Tasks | `Tasks.Metrics` |\n| `ExecSync` / `Exec` | Tasks | `Tasks.Exec` + `Tasks.Start` |\n| `Attach` | Tasks | Streaming via `Tasks.Exec` |\n\n### Request Flow Example: CreateContainer\n\n```\nkubelet\n  \u2502\n  \u25bc CRI gRPC Call\nCreateContainerRequest {\n    pod_sandbox_id: \"abc123\"\n    config: ContainerConfig {...}\n    sandbox_config: PodSandboxConfig {...}\n}\n  \u2502\n  \u25bc containerd CRI Plugin\ncriService.CreateContainer() [container_create.go:60]\n  \u2502\n  \u251c\u2500\u2500\u25b6 Reserve container name\n  \u251c\u2500\u2500\u25b6 Resolve image\n  \u251c\u2500\u2500\u25b6 Build OCI spec\n  \u2502\n  \u25bc containerd Client\nclient.NewContainer() [uses Containers.Create gRPC]\n  \u2502\n  \u25bc\nContainer stored in containerd metadata\n  \u2502\n  \u25bc Response\nCreateContainerResponse {\n    container_id: \"xyz789\"\n}\n```\n\n### Data Flow: Pod Sandbox Lifecycle\n\n```\n1. RunPodSandbox\n # Kubernetes Container Runtime Interface (CRI) Trace Analysis

This document traces the Kubernetes Container Runtime Interface (CRI) from its gRPC service definition in the Kubernetes repository to containerd's implementation.

## Overview

The Container Runtime Interface (CRI) is a plugin interface that enables kubelet to use different container runtimes without needing to recompile. CRI defines a set of gRPC services that any compliant container runtime must implement.

```
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                           KUBERNETES                                     │
│  ┌─────────┐         ┌────────────────┐         ┌─────────────────────┐ │
│  │ kubelet │ ──────> │ CRI gRPC Client│ ──────> │ RuntimeService API  │ │
│  └─────────┘         └────────────────┘         │ (api.proto)         │ │
│                                                  └─────────────────────┘ │
└──────────────────────────────────┬──────────────────────────────────────┘
                                   │ gRPC
                                   ▼
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                           CONTAINERD                                     │
│  ┌─────────────────────┐         ┌────────────────────────────────────┐ │
│  │ CRI Plugin          │ ──────> │ criService Implementation          │ │
│  │ (gRPC Server)       │         │ (internal/cri/server/)             │ │
│  └─────────────────────┘         └────────────────────────────────────┘ │
│                                             │                            │
│                                             ▼                            │
│                      ┌──────────────────────────────────────┐           │
│                  
... (truncated)
